<tr class="mergedrow">
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="border:4px solid #FFE153; line-height: 1.5; text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></div>
</th>

<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Official name</th>
<td>Brasilia</td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Type</th>
<td>Cultural</td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Criteria</th>
<td>i, iv</td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Designated</th>
<td>1987 <small>(11th <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">session</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Reference&#160;no.</th>
<td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://whc.unesco.org/en/list/445">445</a></td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row">Region</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_the_Americas" title="List of World Heritage Sites in the Americas">Latin America and the Caribbean</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Brasília</b> (<small>Portuguese pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[bɾaˈziljɐ]</a></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/Federal_capital" title="Federal capital">federal capital</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seat" title="Seat">seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" title="Forms of government">government</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal District</a>. The city is atop the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_highlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian highlands">Brazilian highlands</a> in the country's <a href="/wiki/Central-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Central-West Region, Brazil">center-western</a> region. It was founded on April 21, 1960, to serve as the new national capital. Brasília and its metro (encompassing the Federal District) had a population of 2,556,149 in 2011, making it Brazil's <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_in_Brazil" title="List of largest cities in Brazil">4th most populous city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Among major Latin American cities, Brasília has the highest GDP per capita at <span style="white-space: nowrap">R$61,915</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$36,175</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brasília was planned and developed by <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BAcio_Costa" title="Lúcio Costa">Lúcio Costa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a> in 1956 to move the capital from <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> to a more central location. The landscape architect was <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Burle_Marx" title="Roberto Burle Marx">Roberto Burle Marx</a>. The city's design divides it into numbered blocks as well as sectors for specified activities, such as the Hotel Sector, the Banking Sector and the Embassy Sector. Brasília was chosen as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> due to its <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist architecture</a> and uniquely artistic urban planning.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The centers of all three branches of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Brazil" title="Federal government of Brazil">federal government of Brazil</a> are in Brasília, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">Congress</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Tribunal" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Federal Tribunal">Supreme Court</a>. The city also hosts 124 foreign <a href="/wiki/Embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassies">embassies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_International_Airport" title="Brasília International Airport">Brasília International Airport</a> connects the capital to all major Brazilian cities and many international destinations, and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Brazil" title="List of the busiest airports in Brazil">third busiest airport in Brazil</a>.</p>
<p>The city has a unique status in Brazil, as it is an administrative division rather than a legal municipality like other <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Brazil">cities in Brazil</a>, similar to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> in the United States and <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a> in Australia. The name 'Brasília' is commonly used as a synonym for the Federal District through <a href="/wiki/Synecdoche" title="Synecdoche">synecdoche</a>; However, the Federal District is composed of <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_regions_in_Federal_District" title="List of administrative regions in Federal District">31 administrative regions</a>, only one of which is Brasília proper, with a population of 214,529 in a 2012 survey; Demographic publications generally do not make this distinction and list the population of Brasília as synonymous with the population of the Federal District, considering the whole as a single city (as Washington, DC), as it was legally before the creation of administrative regions in 1964. For municipal purposes in Brazil, the Federal District is treated as a city-state, single municipality (Brasília), most easily seen in vehicle plates. The city was one of the main host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>. Brasília also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup">2013 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="History of Brasília">History of Brasília</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Timeline of Brasília">Timeline of Brasília</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">History of Brazil</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1763 until 1960, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> was Brazil's capital. At this time, resources tended to be centered in Brazil's southeast region near Rio de Janeiro. Brasília's geographically central location fostered a more regionally neutral federal capital. An article of the country's first <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Constitution_of_1891" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Constitution of 1891">republican constitution</a> dating back to 1891 stated the capital should be moved from Rio de Janeiro to a place close to the country's center.</p>
<p>The plan was conceived in 1827 by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bonif%C3%A1cio" class="mw-redirect" title="José Bonifácio">José Bonifácio</a>, an advisor to Emperor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro I</a>. He presented a plan to the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil#Parliament" title="Empire of Brazil">General Assembly of Brazil</a> for a new city called Brasília, with the idea of moving the capital westward from the heavily populated southeastern corridor. The bill was not enacted because Pedro I dissolved the Assembly.</p>
<p>According to legend, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> saint <a href="/wiki/John_Bosco" title="John Bosco">Don Bosco</a> in 1883 had a dream in which he described a futuristic city that roughly fitted Brasília's location.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In Brasília today, many references of Bosco, who founded the <a href="/wiki/Salesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Salesian">Salesian</a> order, are found throughout the city and one church parish in the city bears his name.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek" title="Juscelino Kubitschek">Juscelino Kubitschek</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a> from 1956 to 1961, ordered Brasília's construction, fulfilling the promise of the Constitution and his own political campaign promise. Building Brasília was part of Juscelino's "fifty years of prosperity in five" plan. Already in 1892, the astronomer <a href="/wiki/Louis_Cruls" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis Cruls">Louis Cruls</a>, in the service of the Brazilian government, had investigated the site for the future capital. <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BAcio_Costa" title="Lúcio Costa">Lúcio Costa</a> won a contest and was the main urban planner in 1957, with 5550 people competing. <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>, a close friend, was the chief architect of most public buildings and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Burle_Marx" title="Roberto Burle Marx">Roberto Burle Marx</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architecture" title="Landscape architecture">landscape designer</a>. Brasília was built in 41 months, from 1956 to April 21, 1960, when it was officially inaugurated.</p>
<p>Until the 1980s, the Federal Government appointed the governor of the Federal District, and the laws of Brasília were issued by the Brazilian Federal Senate. With the Constitution of 1988, Brasília gained the right to elect its <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">Governor</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/District_Assembly" title="District Assembly">District Assembly</a> (Câmara Legislativa) was elected to exercise <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The Federal District does not have a Judicial Power. The Judicial Power which serves the Federal District also serves federal territories. Brazil does not have any territories, therefore, for now the courts only serve cases from the Federal District.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal,_Brasil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg/220px-Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg/330px-Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg/440px-Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal%2C_Brasil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3169" data-file-height="2998" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_parcial_do_Distrito_Federal,_Brasil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brasília from <a href="/wiki/ISS" class="mw-redirect" title="ISS">ISS</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parano.C3.A1_Lake">Paranoá Lake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Paranoá Lake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Parano%C3%A1_Lake" title="Paranoá Lake">Paranoá Lake</a> is a large artificial lake that was built to increase the amount of water available and the region's humidity. It has Brazil's second largest marina, and hosts wakeboarders and windsurfers. Diving can also be practiced and one of the main attractions is Vila Amaury, an old village submerged in the lake. This is where the first construction workers of Brasília used to live.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Brazil" title="Climate of Brazil">Climate of Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brasília has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate (Aw)</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen system</a>, with two distinct seasons: the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season">rainy season</a>, from October to April, and a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, from May to September.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The average temperature is 20.6&#160;°C (69.1&#160;°F). September, at the end of the dry season, has the highest average maximum temperature, 28.3&#160;°C (82.9&#160;°F), has major and minor lower maximum average temperature, of 25.1&#160;°C (77.2&#160;°F) and 12.9&#160;°C (55.2&#160;°F), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-AverageLowC_INMET_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AverageLowC_INMET-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AverageHighC_INMET_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AverageHighC_INMET-12">[12]</a></sup> Average temperatures from September through March are a consistent 22&#160;°C (72&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-DailyMeanC_INMET_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyMeanC_INMET-13">[13]</a></sup> With 247.4&#160;mm (9.7&#160;in), January is the month with the highest rainfall of the year, while June is the lowest, with only 8.7&#160;mm (0.3&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-Rainfall_INMET_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rainfall_INMET-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Brazilian National Institute of Meteorology (INMET), the record low temperature was 1.6&#160;°C (34.9&#160;°F) on July 18, 1975, and the record high was 35.8&#160;°C (96.4&#160;°F) on October 28, 2008. The highest accumulated rainfall in 24 hours was 132.8&#160;mm (5.2&#160;in) on November 15, 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brazil" title="Demographics of Brazil">Demographics of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_eixo_monumental.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Monumental Axis</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">2010 IBGE Census</a>, there were 2,469,489 people residing in Brasília and its metropolitan area,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> of which 1,239,882 were <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Multiracial#Brazil" title="Multiracial">multiracial</a>) (48.2%), 1,084,418, <a href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Brazilian">White</a> (42.2%), 198,072, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">Black</a> (7.7%), 41,522, <a href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian</a> (1.6%), and 6,128 <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Amerindian</a> (0.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Brasília was ranked the fourth most-populous city in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> after <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 2010, the city had 474,871 opposite-sex couples and 1,241 same-sex couples. The population of Brasília was 52.2% <a href="/wiki/Female" title="Female">female</a> and 47.8% <a href="/wiki/Male" title="Male">male</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1960 census there were almost 140 thousand residents in the new Federal District. By 1970 this figure had grown to 537 thousand. By 2000 the population of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal District</a> had surpassed 2 million. The city of Brasília proper was planned for only about 500 thousand inhabitants, but its metropolitan area has grown past this figure.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg/220px-Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg/330px-Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg/440px-Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1062" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bras%C3%ADlia_from_space.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brasília at night from <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the beginning, the growth of Brasília was greater than original estimates. According to the original plans, Brasília would be a city for government authorities and staff. However, during the construction period, Brazilians from all over the country migrated to Brasília, seeking public and private jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the close of the 20th century, Brasília held the distinction of being the largest city in the world which had not existed at the beginning of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Brasília has one of the highest population growth rates in Brazil, with annual growth of 2.82%, mostly due to internal migration.</p>
<p>Brasília's inhabitants include a foreign population of mostly embassy workers as well as large numbers of Brazilian internal migrants. Today, the city has important communities of immigrants and refugees. The city's <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> was 0.936 in 2000 (<a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a> level), and the city's literacy rate was around 95.65%.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Cathedral of Brasília">Cathedral of Brasília</a> in the capital of the Federative Republic of Brazil, is an expression of the architect <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>. This concrete-framed <a href="/wiki/Hyperboloid_structure" title="Hyperboloid structure">hyperboloid structure</a>, seems with its glass roof reaching up, open, to the heavens. On 31 May 1970, the Cathedral's structure was finished, and only the 70&#160;m (229.66&#160;ft) diameter of the circular area were visible. Niemeyer's project of Cathedral of Brasília is based in the <a href="/wiki/Hyperboloid" title="Hyperboloid">hyperboloid</a> of revolution which sections are asymmetric. The hyperboloid structure itself is a result of 16 identical assembled concrete columns. These columns, having hyperbolic section and weighing 90 t, represent two hands moving upwards to heaven. The Cathedral was dedicated on 31 May 1970.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_(vista_lateral).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg/330px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg/440px-Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_%28vista_lateral%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Buriti_(vista_lateral).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brasília city hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresso_Nacional.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Congresso_Nacional.jpg/220px-Congresso_Nacional.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Congresso_Nacional.jpg/330px-Congresso_Nacional.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Congresso_Nacional.jpg/440px-Congresso_Nacional.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2699" data-file-height="1829" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresso_Nacional.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">The National Congress</a> building.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress</a> consists of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Brazil">Senate</a> (the upper house) and the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Brazil">Chamber of Deputies of Brazil</a> (the lower house). Since the 1960s, the National Congress has been located in Brasília.</p>
<p>As with most official buildings throughout the city, it was designed by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a> in the style of modern Brazilian architecture. The hemisphere to the left is the seat of the Senate and the hemisphere to the right is the seat of the Chamber of Deputies. The Congress also occupies various other surrounding buildings, some connected by tunnels.</p>
<p>The National Congress building is located in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Eixo Monumental</a>, the city's main avenue. In front lies a large lawn and reflecting pool. The building faces the <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes" title="Praça dos Três Poderes">Praça dos Três Poderes</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">Supreme Federal Court</a> are located.</p>

<p>Of these, <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Washington D.C.">Washington D.C.</a> were likewise cities planned specifically to be their respective countries' seats of government.</p>

</div>
</div>
<p>At the northwestern end of the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Monumental Axis</a> are federal district and municipal buildings, while at the southeastern end, near the middle shore of Lake Paranoá, stand the executive, judicial, and legislative buildings around the Square of Three Powers, the conceptual heart of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg/170px-BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg/255px-BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg/340px-BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1594" data-file-height="2480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BrasiliaBanNacional.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Flag">Brazilian Flag</a> and the National Congress in spring</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>These and other major structures were designed by Brazilian architect <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>. In the Square of Three Powers, he created as a focal point the dramatic Congressional Palace, which is composed of five parts: twin administrative towers flanked by a large, white concrete dome (the meeting place of the Senate) and by an equally massive concrete bowl (the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Brazil">Chamber of Deputies</a>), which is joined to the dome by an underlying, flat-roofed building.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>A series of low-lying annexes (largely hidden) flank both ends. Also in the square are the glass-faced <a href="/wiki/Planalto_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Planalto Palace">Planalto Palace</a> housing the presidential offices, and the Palace of the Supreme Court. Farther east, on a triangle of land jutting into the lake, is the Palace of the Dawn (Palácio da Alvorada; the presidential residence). Between the federal and civic buildings on the Monumental Axis is the city's cathedral, considered by many to be Niemeyer's finest achievement (see photographs of the interior). The parabolically shaped structure is characterized by its 16 gracefully curving supports, which join in a circle 115 feet (35 meters) above the floor of the nave; stretched between the supports are translucent walls of tinted glass. The nave is entered via a subterranean passage rather than conventional doorways. Other notable buildings are Buriti Palace, <a href="/wiki/Itamaraty_Palace" title="Itamaraty Palace">Itamaraty Palace</a>, the National Theater, and several foreign embassies that creatively embody features of their national architecture. The Brazilian landscape architect <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Burle_Marx" title="Roberto Burle Marx">Roberto Burle Marx</a> designed landmark modernist gardens for some of the principal buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both low-cost and luxury housing were built by the government in the Brasília. The residential zones of the inner city are arranged into <i>superquadras</i> ("superblocks"): groups of apartment buildings along with a prescribed number and type of schools, retail stores, and open spaces. At the northern end of Lake Paranoá, separated from the inner city, is a peninsula with many fashionable homes, and a similar city exists on the southern lakeshore. Originally the city planners envisioned extensive public areas along the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">artificial lake</a>, but during early development private clubs, hotels, and upscale residences and restaurants gained footholds around the water. Set well apart from the city are <a href="/wiki/Satellite_town" title="Satellite town">satellite cities</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Gama,_Federal_District" title="Gama, Federal District">Gama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceil%C3%A2ndia" title="Ceilândia">Ceilândia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taguatinga,_Federal_District" title="Taguatinga, Federal District">Taguatinga</a>, Núcleo Bandeirante, <a href="/wiki/Sobradinho,_Federal_District" title="Sobradinho, Federal District">Sobradinho</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Planaltina,_Federal_District" title="Planaltina, Federal District">Planaltina</a>. These cities, with the exception of Gama and Sobradinho were not planned.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monumental_civic_scale">Monumental civic scale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Monumental civic scale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg/220px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg/330px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg/440px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1529" data-file-height="1019" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_da_Asa_Sul_em_dire%C3%A7%C3%A3o_ao_Lago_Sul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of South Wing (<i>Asa Sul</i>) district.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_torredetv1304_4713.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Monumental Axis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brasilia_TV_Tower" title="Brasilia TV Tower">Brasilia TV Tower</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has been both acclaimed and criticized for its use of <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist architecture</a> on a grand scale and for its somewhat <a href="/wiki/Utopia" title="Utopia">utopian</a> city plan.<sup id="cite_ref-global.britannica.com_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global.britannica.com-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a visit to Brasília, the French writer <a href="/wiki/Simone_de_Beauvoir" title="Simone de Beauvoir">Simone de Beauvoir</a> complained that all of its <i>superquadras</i> exuded "the same air of elegant monotony," and other observers have equated the city's large open lawns, plazas, and fields to wastelands. As the city has matured, some of these have gained adornments, and many have been improved by landscaping, giving some observers a sense of "humanized" spaciousness. Although not fully accomplished, the "Brasília utopia" has produced a city of relatively high quality of life, in which the citizens live in forested areas with sporting and leisure structure (the <i>superquadras</i>) flanked by small commercial areas, bookstores and cafes; the city is famous for its cuisine and efficiency of transit.<sup id="cite_ref-global.britannica.com_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global.britannica.com-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Even these positive features have sparked controversy, expressed in the nickname "ilha da fantasia" ("fantasy island"), indicating the sharp contrast between the city and surrounding regions, marked by poverty and disorganization in the cities of the states of <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A1s" title="Goiás">Goiás</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, around Brasília.<sup id="cite_ref-global.britannica.com_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global.britannica.com-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Critics of Brasília's grand scale have characterized it as a modernist platonic fantasy about the future:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Nothing dates faster than people's fantasies about the future. This is what you get when perfectly decent, intelligent, and talented men start thinking in terms of space rather than place; and single rather than multiple meanings. It's what you get when you design for political aspirations rather than real human needs. You get miles of jerry-built platonic nowhere infested with <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagens</a>. This, one may fervently hope, is the last experiment of its kind. The utopian buck stops here.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hughes_(critic)" title="Robert Hughes (critic)">Robert Hughes</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shock_of_the_New" title="The Shock of the New">The Shock of the New</a></i>, Episode 4: "Trouble in Utopia", (1980)</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Economy of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_setorbancariosul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
South Banking Sector.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The major roles of construction and of services (government, communications, banking and finance, food production, entertainment, and legal services) in Brasília's economy reflect the city's status as a governmental rather than an industrial center. Industries connected with construction, food processing, and furnishings are important, as are those associated with publishing, printing, and computer software. GDP is divided in Public Administration 54.8%, Services 28.7%, Industry 10.2%, Commerce 6.1%, Agribusiness 0.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides being the political center, Brasília is an important economic center. Brasília has the highest city gross domestic product (GDP) of 99.5&#160;billion reais representing 3.76% of the total Brazilian GDP. The main economic activity of the federal capital results from its administrative function. Its industrial planning is studied carefully by the Government of the Federal District. Being a city registered by UNESCO, the government in Brasília has opted to encourage the development of non-polluting industries such as software, film, video, and gemology among others, with emphasis on environmental preservation and maintaining ecological balance, preserving the city property.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a>'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees#Mercer_surveys" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">city rankings of cost of living for expatriate employees</a>, Brasília ranks 45th among the most expensive cities in the world in 2012, up from the 70th position in 2010, ranking behind <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> (12th) and <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> (13th).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg/220px-Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg/330px-Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg/440px-Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Shopping_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shopping center in the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>(91% of local GDP, according to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">IBGE</a>):</p>
<ul>
<li>Government – the public sector is by far the largest employer, accounting for around 40% of the city jobs. Government jobs include all levels, from the federal police to diplomacy, from the transportation bureau to the armed forces;</li>
<li>Communications – the telephony used to be a state monopoly, and Brasília held the HQ of <a href="/wiki/Telebr%C3%A1s" title="Telebrás">Telebrás</a>, the central state company; one of the enterprises that resulted from the privatization of the system in the 90's, <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Telecom" title="Brasil Telecom">Brasil Telecom</a>, keeps it HQ in the city; the official Postal Service (<a href="/wiki/Correios" title="Correios">Correios</a>) HQ is located in the city as well; as it is the main place of Federal Government news, it is also notable the activities of <a href="/wiki/Television_channel" title="Television channel">TV stations</a>, including the main offices of four public networks (<a href="/wiki/TV_Brasil" title="TV Brasil">TV Brasil</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%AAncia_Brasil" title="Agência Brasil">Agência Brasil</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV_C%C3%A2mara" title="TV Câmara">TV Câmara</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV_Senado" title="TV Senado">TV Senado</a> and <a href="/wiki/TV_Justi%C3%A7a" title="TV Justiça">TV Justiça</a>), the regional offices of four major private television networks (<a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Brasileiro_de_Televis%C3%A3o" title="Sistema Brasileiro de Televisão">SBT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rede_Bandeirantes" title="Rede Bandeirantes">Rede Bandeirantes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rede_Record" title="Rede Record">Rede Record</a>) and a main affiliate of <a href="/wiki/RedeTV!" title="RedeTV!">RedeTV!</a>;</li>
<li>Banking and finance – headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Banco_do_Brasil" title="Banco do Brasil">Banco do Brasil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Econ%C3%B4mica_Federal" title="Caixa Econômica Federal">Caixa Econômica Federal</a>, both controlled by the Federal Government, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Brazilian companies">Banco de Brasília</a>, controlled by the city local government; it is also the site of the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank</a>, the main government regulatory agency of the financial sector;</li>
<li>Entertainment – the shopping malls <a href="/wiki/Conjunto_Nacional_(Bras%C3%ADlia)" title="Conjunto Nacional (Brasília)">Conjunto Nacional</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_ParkShopping" title="The ParkShopping">ParkShopping</a>, Pátio Brasil Shopping, Brasília Shopping, Boulevard Shopping, Taguatinga Shopping, Terraço Shopping, Gilberto Salomão and Iguatemi Brasília.</li>
<li>Information technology (<a href="/wiki/Politec" title="Politec">Politec</a>, Poliedro, CTIS, among others), and legal services.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">Industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_torredetveixomonumental.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
South Hotel Sector.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the city include: Construction (Paulo Octavio, Via Construções, and Irmãos Gravia among others); Food processing (Perdigão, Sadia); Furniture Making; <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">Recycling</a> (Novo Rio, <a href="/wiki/Rexam" title="Rexam">Rexam</a>, Latasa and others); <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">Pharmaceuticals</a> (União Química); Graphic industries. The main agricultural products produced in the city are <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guavas" class="mw-redirect" title="Guavas">guavas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strawberry" title="Strawberry">strawberries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papayas" class="mw-redirect" title="Papayas">papayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soy_beans" class="mw-redirect" title="Soy beans">soy beans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mangoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangoes">mangoes</a>. It has over 110,000 cows and it exports wood products worldwide.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal District</a>, where Brasília is located, has a GDP of R$133,4 billion (about US$64.1 billion), about the same as Belarus according to <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>. Its share of the total Brazilian GDP is about 3.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-GDF_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDF-37">[37]</a></sup> The Federal District has the largest <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP per capita</a> income of Brazil US$25,062, slightly higher than Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-GDF_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDF-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's planned design included specific areas for almost everything, including <a href="/wiki/Hotel" title="Hotel">accommodation</a>, Hotels Sectors North and South. New hotel facilities are being developed elsewhere, such as the hotels and tourism Sector North, located on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Parano%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Paranoá">Lake Paranoá</a>. Brasília has a range of tourist accommodation from inns, pensions and hostels to larger international chain hotels. The city's restaurants cater to a wide range of foods from local and regional Brazilian dishes to international cuisine.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brazil" title="Culture of Brazil">Culture of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg/170px-Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg/255px-Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg/340px-Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="2365" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Complexo_Cultural_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cultural_Complex_of_the_Republic" title="Cultural Complex of the Republic">Cultural Complex of the Republic</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a venue for political events, music performances and movie festivals, Brasília is a cosmopolitan city, with around 124 <a href="/wiki/Embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassies">embassies</a>, a wide range of restaurants and complete infrastructure ready to host any kind of event. Not surprisingly, the city stands out as an important business tourism destination, which is an important part of the local economy, with dozens of hotels spread around the federal capital. Traditional parties take place throughout the year.</p>
<p>In June, large festivals known as "<a href="/wiki/Festa_junina" class="mw-redirect" title="Festa junina">festas juninas</a>" are held celebrating <a href="/wiki/List_of_Catholic_saints" title="List of Catholic saints">Catholic saints</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anthony_of_Padua" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Anthony of Padua">Saint Anthony of Padua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_the_Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint John the Baptist">Saint John the Baptist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a>. On September 7, the traditional <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Independence Day">Independence Day</a> parade is held on the Ministries Esplanade. Throughout the year, local, national, and international events are held throughout the city. Christmas is widely celebrated, and <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> usually hosts major events.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city also hosts a varied assortment of art works from artists like <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Giorgi" title="Bruno Giorgi">Bruno Giorgi</a>, Alfredo Ceschiatti, <a href="/wiki/Athos_Bulc%C3%A3o" title="Athos Bulcão">Athos Bulcão</a>, Marianne Peretti, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Volpi" title="Alfredo Volpi">Alfredo Volpi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Di_Cavalcanti" title="Emiliano Di Cavalcanti">Di Cavalcanti</a>, Dyllan Taxman, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Brecheret" title="Victor Brecheret">Victor Brecheret</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burle_Marx" class="mw-redirect" title="Burle Marx">Burle Marx</a>, whose works have been integrated into the city's architecture, making it a unique landscape. The cuisine in the city is very diverse. Many of the best restaurants in the city can be found in the Asa Sul district.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is also the birthplace of Brazilian rock and place of origin of many bands like: <a href="/wiki/Legi%C3%A3o_Urbana" title="Legião Urbana">Legião Urbana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_Inicial" title="Capital Inicial">Capital Inicial</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aborto_El%C3%A9trico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aborto Elétrico (page does not exist)">Aborto Elétrico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plebe_Rude" title="Plebe Rude">Plebe Rude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raimundos" title="Raimundos">Raimundos</a>. Currently Brasília has the Rock Basement Festival who attempts to bring new bands to the national scene. The festival is held in the parking <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_Man%C3%A9_Garrincha" title="Estádio Nacional Mané Garrincha">Brasilia National Stadium Mané Garrincha</a>.</p>
<p>In the local cinema production, Afonso Brazza is an outstanding director who became cult thanks to his low budget police movies. Another filmmaker rooted in Brasilia is Vladimir Carvalho, who is well-known not only in Brasilia but in the whole country. He is also a cinema teacher at University of Brasilia and has produced 21 documentaries, most of them about the capital's history, social culture problems and politics. Since 1965, the annual Brasilia Festival of Brazilian Cinema is one of the most traditional cinema festivals in Brazil, being compared only to the Brazilian Cinema Festival of Gramado, in Rio Grande do Sul. The difference between both is that the festival in Brasilia still preserves the tradition to only submit and reward Brazilian movies.</p>
<p>Brasília has also been the focus of modern-day literature. Published in 2008, <i>The World In Grey: Dom Bosco's Prophecy</i>, by author Ryan J. Lucero, tells an apocalypticle story based on the famous prophecy from the late 19th century by the Italian saint <a href="/wiki/John_Bosco" title="John Bosco">Don Bosco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> According to Don Bosco's prophecy:<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> "Between parallels <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_south" title="15th parallel south">15</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_parallel_south" title="20th parallel south">20</a>, around a lake which shall be formed; A great civilization will thrive, and that will be the Promised Land." Brasília lies between the parallels 15° S and 20° S, where an artificial lake (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Parano%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Paranoá">Paranoá Lake</a>) was formed. Don Bosco is Brasília's <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/American_Flagg!" title="American Flagg!">American Flagg!</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/First_Comics" title="First Comics">First Comics</a> comic book series created by <a href="/wiki/Howard_Chaykin" title="Howard Chaykin">Howard Chaykin</a>, portrays Brasília as a cosmopolitan world capital of culture and exotic romance. In the series, it is a top vacation and party destination. The 2015 <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Felizes_para_Sempre%3F" title="Felizes para Sempre?">Felizes para Sempre?</a></i> was set in Brasília.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sites_and_museums">Historic sites and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Historic sites and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Monumental Axis and Square of the Three Powers</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg/220px-Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg/330px-Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg/440px-Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="378" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes_em_Bras%C3%ADlia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes" title="Praça dos Três Poderes">Praça dos Três Poderes</a> (Three Powers Plaza)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of the <i><a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Eixo Monumental</a></i> ("Monumental Axis") lies the <i>Esplanada dos Ministérios</i> ("Ministries Esplanade"), an open area in downtown Brasília. The rectangular lawn is surrounded by two eight-lane avenues where many government buildings, monuments and memorials are located. On Sundays and holidays, the Eixo Monumental is closed to cars so that locals may use it as a place to walk, bike, and have picnics under the trees.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes" title="Praça dos Três Poderes">Praça dos Três Poderes</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for <i>Square of the Three Powers</i>) is a plaza in Brasília. The name is derived from the encounter of the three federal branches around the plaza: the Executive, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a> (presidential office); the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative</a>, represented by the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress</a> (Congresso Nacional); and the Judicial branch, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court_(Brazil)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Federal Court (Brazil)">Supreme Federal Court</a> (Supremo Tribunal Federal). It is a tourist attraction in Brasília, designed by <a href="/wiki/Lucio_Costa" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucio Costa">Lúcio Costa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a> as a place where the three branches would meet harmoniously.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1508px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of the Monumental Axis"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Brasilia_Panorama.jpg/1500px-Brasilia_Panorama.jpg" width="1500" height="182" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Brasilia_Panorama.jpg/2250px-Brasilia_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Brasilia_Panorama.jpg/3000px-Brasilia_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11774" data-file-height="1425" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Brasilia Panorama.jpg"></a></div>
Panorama of the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Monumental Axis</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>Palaces</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg/220px-Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg/330px-Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg/440px-Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Alvorada_commons.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Alvorada" title="Palácio da Alvorada">Palácio da Alvorada</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Planalto_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/220px-Planalto_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/330px-Planalto_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/440px-Planalto_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="2840" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Planalto_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Alvorada" title="Palácio da Alvorada">Palácio da Alvorada</a> is the official residence of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a>. The palace was designed, along with the rest of the city of Brasília, by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a> and inaugurated in 1958. One of the first structures built in the republic's new capital city, the "Alvorada" lies on a peninsula at the margins of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Parano%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Paranoá">Lake Paranoá</a>. The principles of simplicity and modernity, that in the past characterized the great works of architecture, motivated Niemeyer. The viewer has an impression of looking at a glass box, softly landed on the ground with the support of thin external columns. The building has an area of 7,000 m<sup>2</sup> with three floors consisting of the basement, landing, and second floor. The auditorium, kitchen, laundry, medical center, and administration offices are at basement level. The rooms used by the presidency for official receptions are on the landing. The second floor has four suites, two apartments, and various private rooms which make up the residential part of the palace. The building also has a library, a heated Olympic-sized swimming pool, a music room, two dining rooms and various meeting rooms. A chapel and heliport are in adjacent buildings.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a> is the official workplace of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a>. It is located at the <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_dos_Tr%C3%AAs_Poderes" title="Praça dos Três Poderes">Praça dos Três Poderes</a> in Brasília. As the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Brazil" title="Politics of Brazil">seat of government</a>, the term "Planalto" is often used as a <a href="/wiki/Metonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Metonym">metonym</a> for the executive branch of government. The main working office of the President of the Republic is in the Palácio do Planalto. The President and his or her family do not live in it, rather in the official residence, the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Alvorada" title="Palácio da Alvorada">Palácio da Alvorada</a>. Besides the President, senior advisors also have offices in the "Planalto," including the <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice-President of Brazil">Vice-President of Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Staff_of_Brazil" title="Chief of Staff of Brazil">Chief of Staff</a>. The other Ministries are along the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Esplanada dos Ministérios</a>. The architect of the Palácio do Planalto was <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>, creator of most of the important buildings in Brasília. The idea was to project an image of simplicity and modernity using fine lines and waves to compose the columns and exterior structures. The Palace is four stories high, and has an area of 36,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>. Four other adjacent buildings are also part of the complex.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IB_UnB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/IB_UnB.jpg/220px-IB_UnB.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/IB_UnB.jpg/330px-IB_UnB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/IB_UnB.jpg/440px-IB_UnB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IB_UnB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Institute of Biological Sciences (IB) of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="University of Brasília">University of Brasília</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Brazil" title="Education in Brazil">Education in Brazil</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a> is the official national language and the primary language taught in schools. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> are also part of the official curriculum. The city has six <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international schools</a>: <a href="/wiki/American_School_of_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="American School of Brasília">American School of Brasília</a>, Brasília International School (BIS), Escola das Nações, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss International School">Swiss International School</a> (SIS), Lycée français François-Mitterrand (LfFM) and Maple Bear Canadian School.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> August 2016 will see the opening of a new international school - <a href="/wiki/The_British_School_of_Brasilia" class="mw-redirect" title="The British School of Brasilia">The British School of Brasilia</a>. Brasília has two universities, three university centers, and many private colleges.</p>
<p>The main tertiary educational institutions are: <a href="/wiki/Universidade_de_Bras%C3%ADlia" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidade de Brasília">Universidade de Brasília</a> – University of Brasília (UnB) (public); <a href="/wiki/Universidade_Cat%C3%B3lica_de_Bras%C3%ADlia" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidade Católica de Brasília">Universidade Católica de Brasília</a> – Catholic University of Brasília (UCB); <a href="/wiki/Centro_Universit%C3%A1rio_de_Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Centro Universitário de Brasília">Centro Universitário de Brasília</a> (UniCEUB); Centro Universitário Euroamaricano (Unieuro); Centro Universitário do Distrito Federal (UDF); Universidade Paulista (UNIP); and Instituto de Educação Superior de Brasília (IESB).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aeroportojk_inauguracaoalasul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_International_Airport" title="Brasília International Airport">Brasília International Airport (BSB)</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg/220px-Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg/330px-Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg/440px-Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_aerea_aeroporto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of the airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_International_Airport" title="Brasília International Airport">Brasília–Presidente Juscelino Kubitschek International Airport</a> serves the metropolitan area with major domestic and international flights. It is the third busiest <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> airport based on passengers and aircraft movements.<sup id="cite_ref-pax_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pax-44">[44]</a></sup> Because of its strategic location it is a civil aviation hub for the rest of the country.</p>
<p>This makes for a large number of takeoffs and landings and it is not unusual for flights to be delayed in the holding pattern before landing. Following the airport's master plan, <a href="/wiki/Infraero" title="Infraero">Infraero</a> built a second runway, which was finished in 2006. In 2007, the airport handled 11,119,872 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-pax_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pax-44">[44]</a></sup> The main building's third floor, with 12 thousand square meters, has a panoramic deck, a food court, shops, four movie theatres with total capacity of 500 people, and space for exhibitions. Brasília Airport has 136 vendor spaces. The airport is located about 11&#160;km (6.8&#160;mi) from the central area of Brasília, outside the metro system. The area outside the airport's main gate is lined with taxis as well as several bus line services which connect the airport to Brasília's central district. The parking lot accommodates 1,200 cars.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The airport is serviced by domestic and regional airlines (TAM, GOL, Azul, WebJET, Trip and Avianca), in addition to a number of international carriers. In 2012, Brasília's International Airport was won by the InfrAmerica consortium, formed by the Brazilian engineering company ENGEVIX and the Argentine Corporacion America holding company, with a 50% stake each.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> During the 25-year concession, the airport may be expanded to up to 40 million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, the airport received 15 new boarding bridges, totalling 28 in all. This was the main requirement made by the federal government, which transferred the operation of the terminal to the Inframerica Group after an auction. The group invested R$750 million in the project. In the same year, the number of <a href="/wiki/Parking" title="Parking">parking</a> spaces doubled, reaching three thousand. The airport's entrance have a new rooftop cover and a new access road. Furthermore, a <a href="/wiki/VIP_room" class="mw-redirect" title="VIP room">VIP room</a> was created on Terminal 1's third floor. The investments resulted an increase the capacity of Brasília's airport from approximately 15 million passengers per year to 21 million by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Brasília has direct flights to all <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">states of Brazil</a> and direct <a href="/wiki/International_flight" title="International flight">international flights</a> to <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panama City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_transport">Road transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Road transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
