The <a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek_bridge" title="Juscelino Kubitschek bridge">Juscelino Kubitschek Bridge</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_(15232674849).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg/220px-Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg/330px-Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg/440px-Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_%2815232674849%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3184" data-file-height="2120" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Esplanada_dos_Minist%C3%A9rios_(15232674849).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Traffic crawls at the Ministries Esplanade.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like most Brazilian cities, Brasilia has a good network of taxi companies. Taxis from the airport are available immediately outside the terminal, but at times there can be quite a queue of people. Although the airport is not far from the downtown area, taxi prices do seem to be higher than in other Brazilian cities. Booking in advance can be advantageous, particularly if time is limited, and local companies should be able to assist airport transfer or transport requirements.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek_bridge" title="Juscelino Kubitschek bridge">Juscelino Kubitschek bridge</a>, also known as the 'President JK Bridge' or the 'JK Bridge', crosses <a href="/wiki/Lake_Parano%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Paranoá">Lake Paranoá</a> in Brasília. It is named after <a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek_de_Oliveira" class="mw-redirect" title="Juscelino Kubitschek de Oliveira">Juscelino Kubitschek de Oliveira</a>, former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">president of Brazil</a>. It was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Chan" title="Alexandre Chan">Alexandre Chan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Structural_engineer" title="Structural engineer">structural engineer</a> Mário Vila Verde. Chan won the <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Lindenthal" title="Gustav Lindenthal">Gustav Lindenthal</a> Medal<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> for this project at the 2003 International Bridge Conference in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> due to "...outstanding achievement demonstrating harmony with the environment, aesthetic merit and successful community participation".</p>
<p>It consists of three 60&#160;m (200&#160;ft) tall asymmetrical steel arches that crisscross diagonally. With a length of 1,200&#160;m (0.75 miles), it was completed in 2002 at a cost of US$56.8&#160;million. The bridge has a pedestrian walkway and is accessible to bicyclists and skaters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Metro</dt>
</dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_Metro" title="Brasília Metro">Brasília Metro</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg/220px-Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg/330px-Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg/440px-Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metro_DF_Galeria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_Metro" title="Brasília Metro">Brasília Metro</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_Metro" title="Brasília Metro">Metrô de Brasília</a> is Brasília's underground <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro system</a>. The subway system has 24 stations on two lines, the Orange and Green lines, distributed along a total network of 42&#160;km (26&#160;mi), covering some of the metropolitan area. Both lines begin at the Central Station and run parallel until the Águas Claras Station. The Brasília metro is not comprehensive, so buses may provide better access to the city centre.</p>
<p>The metro leaves the Rodoviária (bus station) and goes south, avoiding most of the political and tourist areas. The main purpose of the metro is to serve cities, such as Samambaia, <a href="/wiki/Taguatinga,_Federal_District" title="Taguatinga, Federal District">Taguatinga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceil%C3%A2ndia" title="Ceilândia">Ceilândia</a>, as well as Guará and Águas Claras. The satellite cities served are more populated in total than the Plano Piloto itself (the census of 2000 indicated that <a href="/wiki/Ceil%C3%A2ndia" title="Ceilândia">Ceilândia</a> had 344,039 inhabitants, Taguatinga had 243,575, whereas the Plano Piloto had approximately 400,000 inhabitants), and most residents of the satellite cities depend on public transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Brazil" title="High-speed rail in Brazil">high-speed railway</a> was planned between Brasília and Goiânia, the capital of the state of Goias, although it will probably be turned into a regional service linking these capital cities and cities in between, like Anápolis and Alexânia.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg/220px-Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg/330px-Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg/440px-Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1020" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodovi%C3%A1ria_do_Plano_Piloto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Central Bus Station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main bus hub in Brasília is the Central Bus Station, located in the crossing of the <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Axis" title="Monumental Axis">Eixo Monumental</a> and the Eixão, about 2&#160;km (1.2&#160;mi) from the Three Powers Plaza. The original plan was to have a bus station as near as possible to every corner of Brasília. Today, the bus station is the hub of urban buses only, some running within Brasília and others connecting Brasília to the satellite cities.</p>
<p>In the original city plan, the interstate buses should also stop at the Central Station. Because of the growth of Brasília (and corresponding growth in the bus fleet), today the interstate buses leave from the older interstate station (called Rodoferroviária), located at the western end of the Eixo Monumental. The Central Bus Station also contains a main metro station. A new bus station was opened in July 2010. It is on Saída Sul (South Exit) near Parkshopping Mall and with its metro station, and it's also an inter-state bus station, used only to leave the Federal District.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg/220px-Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg/330px-Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg/440px-Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Stadium_-_June_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Estadio_Nacional_de_Brasilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Estadio Nacional de Brasilia">Estádio Nacional de Brasília</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The three most well known teams of Brasília are: <a href="/wiki/Brasiliense_Futebol_Clube" title="Brasiliense Futebol Clube">Brasiliense FC</a> from Taguatinga (Commonly called <i>Jacaré</i>, the "Caiman"); <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_Esportiva_do_Gama" title="Sociedade Esportiva do Gama">SE Gama</a> (Commonly called <i>Verdão</i>, the "Big Green") and <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia_Futebol_Clube" title="Brasília Futebol Clube">Brasília FC</a> (Commonly called <i>Colorado</i>, <i>The Reds</i>). Gama and Brasiliense won the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_B" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série B">Série B</a> of the Brazilian Football Championship once (Gama in 1998 and Brasiliense in 2004), but they failed to be successful in the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Série A</a>. Brasília FC won the regional tournament <a href="/wiki/Copa_Verde" title="Copa Verde">Copa Verde</a> in 2014.</p>
<p>The main stadiums are the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_Man%C3%A9_Garrincha" title="Estádio Nacional Mané Garrincha">Brasilia National Stadium Mané Garrincha</a> (which was reinaugurated on May 18, 2013), the <a href="/wiki/Serej%C3%A3o" title="Serejão">Serejão Stadium</a> (home for Brasiliense) and the <a href="/wiki/Bezerr%C3%A3o" title="Bezerrão">Bezerrão Stadium</a> (home for Gama).</p>
<p>Brasília was one of the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup">2013 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>, for which <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> is the host nation. Brasília hosted the opening of the Confederations Cup and hosted 7 World Cup games.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Brasília will also host football tournaments during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> to be held in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bras%C3%ADlia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg/220px-GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg/330px-GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg/440px-GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GinasioNilsonNelson01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Nilson_Nelson_Gymnasium" title="Nilson Nelson Gymnasium">Nilson Nelson Gymnasium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brasília is known as a departing point for the practice of unpowered <a href="/wiki/Air_sports" title="Air sports">air sports</a>, sports that may be practiced with <a href="/wiki/Hang_gliding" title="Hang gliding">hang gliding</a> or paragliding wings. Practitioners of such sports reveal that, because of the city's dry weather, the city offers strong thermal winds and great "<a href="/wiki/Cloud_street" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloud street">cloud-streets</a>", which is also the name for a manoeuvre quite appreciated by practitioners. In 2003, Brasília hosted the 14th Hang Gliding World Championship, one of the categories of free flying. In August 2005, the city hosted the 2nd stage of the Brazilian Hang Gliding Championship.</p>
<p>Brasília is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Internacional_Nelson_Piquet_(Bras%C3%ADlia)" title="Autódromo Internacional Nelson Piquet (Brasília)">Autódromo Internacional Nelson Piquet</a> which hosted a non-championship round of the <a href="/wiki/1974_Formula_One_season" title="1974 Formula One season">1974 Formula One Grand Prix season</a>. An <a href="/wiki/IndyCar" class="mw-redirect" title="IndyCar">IndyCar</a> race was cancelled at the last minute in 2015.</p>
<p>The city is also home to Uniceub BRB, one of Brazil's best basketball clubs. Currently, <a href="/wiki/Novo_Basquete_Brasil" title="Novo Basquete Brasil">NBB</a> champion (2010, 2011 and 2012). The club hosts some of its games at the 16,000 all-seat <a href="/wiki/Nilson_Nelson_Gymnasium" title="Nilson Nelson Gymnasium">Nilson Nelson Gymnasium</a>.</p>
